Automobile News

Essay

Oil Brake

--- Ding

I have repeatedly been asked by friends about the principle and operation of oil brakes. I am writing this article in response and to bring it to the attention of those in the automotive industry.

Oil brakes (Hydraulic Brake) are commonly known as oil brakes. Cars such as Auburn, Chrysler, Plymouth, DeSoto, Graham, Dodge, and Reo all use it. Almost 30% of American-made cars use oil brakes. It can be seen that this machine is very popular.

The advantages of oil brakes include (1) simplicity (2) sensitivity (3) consistent braking force (4) no vibration noise from metal rods (5) no need for lubricating oil (6) no need for correction, etc. Compared with ordinary rod-pulled brakes, it is much better. The disadvantages are two: (1) the front and rear wheels brake at the same time (2) the braking effect is lost when oil leaks.

The principle of oil brakes is completely based on the fluid transmission method in physics. Any liquid does not shrink in volume due to pressure. When a certain amount of pressure is applied to the liquid, the liquid can transmit the same amount of pressure to where it reaches. This is illustrated in detail in the diagrams. The symbols used in each diagram are the same.

The first diagram shows the simplest structure of an oil brake. W is the brake pedal, P is the master piston, C is the master oil tank, T is the oil pipe, A is the small oil tank, B is the small piston, D is the cone, F is the front wheel, R is the rear wheel, S is the brake shoe, and L is the brake band. When the foot presses down on the master piston, the oil in the master oil tank is forced out and injected into the small oil tank through the oil pipe, pushing the small piston and lowering the cone, opening the brake shoes and pressing tightly on the K brake drum. The wheel is then clamped and stopped from rotating. When the pressure on the brake pedal is removed, the J spring contracts and returns to its original state, allowing the wheel to be free.

First Diagram

The second diagram shows the layout of the oil brake on the car chassis. M is the oil storage tank, used to replenish oil when there is a shortage. C is connected to the master oil tank, which is detailed in the third diagram. The top of the oil storage tank has a H handle, which is used to pump pressure to replenish oil to the master oil tank C. However, like Dodge cars, the oil storage tank and master oil tank are now combined into one, and there is no need to manually pump pressure, and the oil can be replenished to the master oil tank automatically. Just keep half a tank of oil in the oil storage tank. W is the brake pedal. The thick black line is the copper oil pipe, fixed to the chassis. N is a soft rubber pipe, one end connected to the copper pipe and the other end connected to the small oil tank. Therefore, this section must move with the wheel, so rubber pipes must be used. K is the brake drum. When the brake pedal is pressed down with the foot, the oil in the master oil tank is squeezed out and injected into the oil pipe, reaching all four wheels to perform its braking work.

Second Diagram

Third Diagram

The fourth diagram shows the detailed structure of the braking part of the oil brake. This is a contracting brake. The L brake band is on the outer ring of the K brake drum, but there are also expanding ones, that is, the brake band is placed on the inner ring of the brake drum. Its function is the same and will not be repeated. As shown in the diagram, when oil is injected from the N pipe, it pushes the small piston in the A tank outwards, pushing the E lever on both sides, which simultaneously tightens the L brake band, clamping the rotation of the brake drum K. When the oil pressure disappears, the J spring opens, causing the brake band and small piston to return to their original state. The bo in the lower part of the diagram represents the contents of tank A. There are two small pistons inside as the oil inlet, which is connected to the N soft rubber pipe. is the normal state. The two small pistons are lying in the tank. b is the braking state. The oil has been injected. The two small pistons are pushed and rushed out to both ends.

Fourth Diagram

The oil for oil brakes is a mixture of equal parts of castor oil and denatured alcohol. There are ready-made mixes available on the market. Its properties must be such that it is not easy to freeze, not easy to evaporate, and non-corrosive.

The usual attention to oil brakes is to prevent leakage. The places where oil leaks are mostly at the connection between the copper pipe and the rubber pipe. If you usually feel that the oil consumption is too high, there must be a leak. You can have one person step heavily on the brake pedal and another person check where the oil pipe goes to find the leak and repair it.

The small oil tank of the oil brake is not easy to damage. Its structure is very delicate. It must be disassembled with special tools. It is not necessary to disassemble it during repairs. If it is determined to be damaged, there are also complete existing goods that can be matched. Otherwise, it is a waste of effort.

After the oil brake has been repaired or the rubber pipe has been replaced, there is a very important job that cannot be ignored, that is, air must not be allowed to remain in the oil pipe. The volume of air can expand and contract. Leaving it in the oil pipe will cause uneven oil pressure, which is a major drawback. There is a vent on the small oil tank. Usually it is blocked with a screw. Open this hole first when venting. Step on the brake pedal a few times to see if the oil ejected from the hole no longer has air bubbles. This means that the air has been completely discharged. This job.

Page 18

Vent one brake each time, and then take turns to the others. Do not vent all four brakes at the same time. Also, after the brake drum has been removed, do not step on the brake pedal, otherwise the small piston in the small oil tank may be pushed out, damaging important parts.

New Nash Car of 1931

--- Ji Ren

There are three types of eight-cylinder cars and one type of six-cylinder car

At a time when the world's finances are tight and business competition is fierce, the automotive industry is indeed affected infinitely. The American Nash Automobile Manufacturing Plant, in view of this, has improved the 1931 New Nash car and increased the original cost in order to make the selling price of the new car more favorable than other cars. Nash's cars have all achieved this goal. A total of four new products have been released. The following is a brief description of their general situation.

The No. 90 Big Eight-Cylinder Car is the most powerful car manufactured by Nash. It drives quickly and steadily, and is beautifully decorated. Beautiful people study the beauty of car styles and choose the No. 90 long and large New Nash car. 115 horsepower, number-fire engine, eight straight cylinders. It is the most economical to use when it is new. It is most suitable as a personal means of transportation. The exterior and interior of the No. 90 car are novel and the paint colors are bright. It is installed on wheelbases of 124 hours and 133 hours. The interior is beautiful and pleasing to the eye. The exam is complete and considerate. There are eight styles in total. The action is extremely sensitive. Therefore. In today's world, it is welcomed by millions of people every day. The No. 80 Eight-Cylinder Car is the most exquisite of today's overhead valve straight eight-cylinder cars with dual ignition heads. Although the body is smaller than the larger one, its appearance is no different. As for the power action, it is also very strong. The dual-ignition engine can generate 85 horsepower. Wheelbase is 121 inches. The interior and exterior craftsmanship are exquisite. I am sure you will feel that buying it will add luster. The completeness of the car's features and the savings in its cost are rare in cars with such a low price.

The No. 70 Eight-Cylinder Car is the lowest-priced and smallest eight-cylinder car manufactured in the United States. It is also the most complete in features and the most economical in cost. The wheel is 116 hours and a quarter. 75 horsepower. The high-pressure nine-slip engine has a diameter of two inches and seven-eighths. The stroke is four inches and eight-eighths of an inch. It drives steadily and appropriately on all kinds of road surfaces. Comparable to an expensive car. The small eight-cylinder car comes in four styles. No. 870 is a four-door five-seater sedan. No. 877 is a four-door five-seater sedan. No. 872 is a large two-seater sedan (and No. 872 R is a four-seater sedan. Nash's new six-cylinder car is the most affordable and beautiful of Nash's products. The new 1931 model is the culmination of Nash's annual six-cylinder cars. There are five types of cars in total. The styles are very grand. The wheels are all 114 inches and a quarter. No. 660 is a large four-door five-seater sedan. No. 663 is a two-door five-seater sedan. No. 662 is a two-seater sedan. There is a spacious storage area in the rear. No. 662

2 is a four-seater sedan coupe. No. 668 is a five-seater hatchback. "The new Nash six-cylinder car's high-pressure and powerful engine has seven large total sliders, a diameter of three inches and one-eighth, and a stroke of four inches and eight-eighths, producing 60 horsepower. It is equipped with hydraulic shock absorbers at the front and rear. Automatic four-wheel brakes. Completely sealed. Easy to drive. The beautiful contours are beyond the reach of even high-priced cars.

Now that the new Nash has been released, it has been enthusiastically welcomed by people from all over the world. Because it is cheap and beautiful, even in this autumn of commercial and economic panic, it should not be greatly affected.

General Situation of the Jiangsu-Jurong Road Project

— Chong

The Jiangsu-Jurong Road in Jiangsu Province is a total of forty-eight and a half li in length. The roadbed has already been built. The cost of building bridges and culverts, as well as paving the road surface, is estimated to be 172,285 yuan. In addition, 60,000 yuan is required to purchase light railways, totaling over 230,000 yuan. The entire road is currently divided into approximately four sections. The first section is from Paiwan to Fengfeng Nunnery, 7.13 kilometers. The second section is from Fengfeng Nunnery to Shitan Kiln, 10.70 kilometers. The third section is from Shitan Kiln to Luoyang Temple, 10.78 kilometers. The fourth section is from Luoyang Bridge to the East Gate of Jurong, 12.08 kilometers. Currently, the paving of the road surface from Paiwan in Zhenjiang to Fengfeng Nunnery was contracted to the Miao Shunxing Construction Company in August of this year. The construction cost is a total of 27,319 yuan, and the deadline for completion is December 30 of this year. The repair of the roadbed and soilwork, as well as the construction of culverts, is also contracted to the same company, at an estimated cost of 2,597.10 yuan, it is said.
